Example 19: The reporting of a fully repaid instrument incurring no write-off
An instrument which is reported to AnaCredit for the reporting reference dates from
31 December to 28 February is fully repaid on 14 March.
The instrument does not incur any loss in the period concerned.
Consequently, the instrument is not reported to AnaCredit as of 31 March and the last
record available in AnaCredit relates to 28 February.
Furthermore, the last quarterly information available for the instrument goes back to
31 December.
Example 20: The reporting of partially repaid instruments incurring no write-off
A debtor has only one non-revolving instrument.
On 31 January the debtor’s commitment amount is €27,000 vis-à-vis the observed
agent and the instrument is reported to AnaCredit at the reporting reference date.
On 17 February, the debtor makes a payment (e.g. of €5,000), which results in the
debtor’s commitment amount falling below the reporting threshold. The debtor’s
commitment amount does not increase thereafter. In this case, the instrument is not
reported as of 28 February or as of 31 March.
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 89
31 May 2019
Example 21: The reporting of partially securitised instruments
A debtor has only one instrument. As of 31 January the debtor’s commitment amount is
€40,000 vis-à-vis the observed agent and the instrument is reported to AnaCredit.
As of 14 February part of the instrument is subject to securitisation, in which €20,000 is
transferred in a true sale to a special purpose vehicle (SPV). The observed agent keeps
the servicing rights of the transferred part of the instrument.
In this case, the partial transfer does not reduce the outstanding nominal amount (see
Section 4.4.3 in Part II of the Manual) and the debtor’s commitment amount is still
€40,000, even after the transfer.
Consequently, the reporting of the instrument continues after the transfer date.
Example 22: The reporting of sold instruments incurring no write-off
A debtor has only one instrument.
As of 31 March the debtor’s commitment amount is €80,000 vis-à-vis the observed
agent and the instrument is reported to AnaCredit.
On 9 April the instrument is sold to a third party. The observed agent does not keep the
servicing rights of the sold instrument.
In this case, the observed agent neither holds nor services the instrument after the sale.
Furthermore, as the observed agent does not incur a loss that needs to be captured in
AnaCredit (i.e. no write-off), the observed agent does not report the instrument after the
sale (see Section 3.1.6 in Part II of the Manual).

6 Concept of credit, data model and
reportable datasets
1 This chapter addresses the concept of credit which is modelled by distinguishing
2 between three main building blocks: instrument, protection and counterparty.
3 The concept of credit is not just a data model but a whole conceptual model
4 describing how a credit is conceived for the purpose of AnaCredit.
5 After introducing the concept of credit, the chapter discusses how the concept of
6 credit is translated into reportable datasets and looks at the mutual relationships
7 between the reportable datasets. The description is threefold: first the conceptual
8 data model is discussed, then the logical data model is described, and finally the
9 specific datasets are explained on the basis of the data model.
6.1 Conceptual data model
10 The concept of credit is not just a Conceptually, the AnaCredit data model recognises three interconnected data
data model but a whole conceptual
11 entities (i.e. groups of data) related to a credit (e.g. a loan) which differ with regard to
model on how a credit is conceived
12 for the purpose of AnaCredit the data that need to be reported. These data entities are the instrument entity of the
13 credit, the protection entity of the credit and the counterparty entity of the credit.
Revision mark: the term “(data)
entity” is added and used
14 interchangeably with “part”
throughout this section
6.1.1 Concept of credit in the context of AnaCredit
15 Granular reporting to AnaCredit means that data are compiled and reported on the
16 basis of an individual credit, whereby three interrelated data entities (i.e. parts of
17 data on the credit) are distinguished.
18 In fact, the AnaCredit requirements are set out on the basis of an abstract model
19 which, at any given moment in time, represents a running credit instrument extended
20 on the basis of a contract.
21 Specifically, for the purpose of AnaCredit each instrument is assumed to be set up or
22 established on the basis of a contract (commonly referred to as a loan agreement).
23 This basis is reflected in Articles 1(22) and (23) of the AnaCredit Regulation, where
24 contract and instrument are defined. In fact, instruments are defined as specific
25 types of credit granted under a contract.
26 The abstract model underlying the AnaCredit data model has been chosen to
27 broadly reflect the general information describing credit transactions. Contracts (loan
28 or factoring agreements, for example) typically provide the terms and conditions
29 under which a creditor provides credit to a debtor, specifying for instance the amount
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 92
31 May 2019
1 of the credit, the interest charged, the repayment schedule, the conditions of the
2 credit and the representations, warranties and covenants of each party, as well as
3 taking into account the possibility that the features may change from one moment to
4 the next.
5 Revision mark: references to Generally, the AnaCredit reporting requirements involve only three data entities (i.e.
“contract” are added to emphasise
6 parts of data) which are deemed to be the main pillars of any credit granted under a
that instruments are created by
7 contracts contract. These parts are:
(a) the instrument (extended on the basis of a contract) that represents the
individual credit;
(b) the protection that secures the instrument;
(c) the counterparties that are related to or otherwise affiliated with the
instrument and the protection.
8 This means that AnaCredit requires granular information about contracts on an
9 instrument-by-instrument (commonly referred to as loan-by-loan) basis. Furthermore,
10 as each of the above-mentioned parts is characterised by a number of features, the
11 requirements of AnaCredit consist of a number of data attributes that capture certain
12 features of the specific parts of a credit arising under a contract (cf. Section 6.2.2 for
13 more details on data attributes). In fact, once a credit granted by a credit institution is
14 subject to reporting pursuant to the AnaCredit Regulation, 88 data attributes (i.e.
15 individual characteristics of the credit) are in principle required to be reported.
16 Revision marks: further Although from an IT perspective a credit (loan) is merely broken down into the three
clarifications are added in this
17 interconnected data entities (instruments, protection items and counterparties), in
paragraph
18 general terms this concept of credit has fundamental implications for how real-life
19 credit is considered for the purpose of AnaCredit. More specifically, this concept of
20 credit implies that the instrument entity of a credit is kept separate from the
21 protection entity, which is of particular relevance for products that contain embedded
22 protection (cf. Example 25 below and Section 3.4.1 in Part II of the Manual regarding
23 the instrument type “reverse repurchase agreements”). Although these products are
24 not commonly referred to as secured loans, the different data to be reported to
25 AnaCredit are in fact, under this basic premise, broken down into an instrument
26 entity (i.e. a set of data attributes with the specific information on the instrument) and
27 a protection received “entity” (i.e. a set of data attributes with the specific information
28 on the protection received). Moreover, information about who is involved in the credit
29 is placed outside the instrument/protection bracket. Counterparties are explicitly
30 distinguished from one another and clearly identified in relation to the instrument or
31 the protection.
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 93
31 May 2019
Example 25: Reverse repurchase agreements – perspective of the buyer
Reverse repurchase agreements (reverse repos) are transactions in which an institution
lends cash in exchange for financial assets sold by the owner of the financial assets at
a given price under a commitment by the owner of the financial assets to repurchase
the same (or identical) assets at a fixed price on a specified future date.
Broadly speaking, a reverse repurchase agreement is a transaction concluded on the
deal date between two parties, the institution and the owner of the financial assets, in
which:
• the owner of the financial assets sells a specified financial asset to the institution at
an agreed price on date T1;
• the owner will repurchase the same (or identical) financial assets from the
institution at a price agreed on the deal date on date T2 (after T1).
Reverse repurchase agreement for the institution buying financial assets
Date T1
Financial assets
Financial asset
Institution
owner
Cash
Date T2
Financial assets
Financial asset
Institution
owner
Cash + repo interest
While the mechanics of a reverse repo involve selling and then repurchasing securities
at a set price and a set time, at its financial essence, a reverse repo is in essence a
collateralised loan.
Using this broader concept of credit, a reverse repo transaction is broken down into the
three pillars – the instrument part, the protection part and the counterparty part. In this
example, the instrument is the cash loaned out to the owner of the financial asset, while
the financial asset, which in essence collateralises the instrument, is the protection item,
and the counterparty part comprises the institution (the creditor) and the owner of the
financial asset (the debtor), which by providing the financial asset as implicit protection
to the creditor also functions as the protection provider.
Although a (reverse) repo transaction (where the financial asset is sold and later
repurchased) is conceptually modelled in exactly the same way as a collateralised loan
(where the financial asset is instead pledged as collateral for a loan), the two types of
transaction can be clearly distinguished through the information contained in AnaCredit
(more specifically, by the type of instrument).
1 In practice, the granular reporting of credit means that for each credit granted by
2 credit institutions, AnaCredit broadly requires instrument, protection and
3 debtor/creditor information. Please refer to Section 6.3 for more details on the data
4 elements that are required.
5 Using data modelling terminology, a credit is modelled as a collection of data entities
6 and relationships among data entities. In particular, the three parts of a credit are an
7 information triple that characterises the credit.
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 94
31 May 2019
1 Revision mark: this paragraph is In the conceptual data model of credit, the distinct parts into which the data are
expanded with further clarifications
2 grouped on the basis of their nature are referred to as data “entities”. Consequently,
about “(data) entities”
3 a data entity is a group of data that is distinguishable from other groups of data
4 relating to the credit. The three data entities of the AnaCredit data model are:
(a) the instrument entity;
(b) the protection entity;
(c) the counterparty entity.
5 A brief description of these credit data entities is presented below. More details,
6 including the data attributes, are provided in the subsequent sections and in Part II of
7 the Manual.
6.1.2 Instrument
8 The instrument entity is at the heart of a credit. This data entity contains the
9 information about the individual credit, i.e. individual commitments with unique terms
10 under a credit agreement such as product type, maturity date, interest rate, etc.
11 Instruments arise under a contract, and for each instrument there is always a debtor,
12 a creditor and a servicer. Several instruments may be part of the same contract.
13 When defining a data model to capture instruments, it should be taken into account
14 that there may be multiple debtors of the same instrument. This implies that such
15 instruments theoretically function as the instrument entity in multiple triples (of
16 instrument, protection and counterparty). The same instrument would therefore
17 appear in several triples, with each instrument entity relating to a different debtor.
18 This implies that part of (or all) of the information relating to the instrument provided
19 in each entry could be specific to the participation of the debtor in that instrument
20 and not common across debtors.18 Generally, the data model is designed so that
21 there is no duplication of reportable information – part of the information would be
22 common across the debtors (in the instrument dataset) and another part of it specific
23 to the participation of the debtor (in the counterparty-instrument dataset). Please
24 refer to Section 6.2 for details regarding how the information is effectively organised
25 in the context of AnaCredit.
26 In the context of AnaCredit, instruments are reported gross of any protection
27 securing the instrument.
18 Entry-specific information refers to the three positions in a triple set (instrument, protection item,
counterparty) that describes a given credit transaction. This means that an instrument (or
protection item or counterparty) may occupy the position of the instrument entity (or protection
entity or counterparty entity) in multiple such triples referring to multiple credit transactions.
However, there is just one record for each instrument, protection item and counterparty. This is
because these records are the building blocks that may be combined via the identifiers to form
an unlimited number of such triple sets. Ultimately, the data model is designed so that there is no
duplication of reportable records.
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 95
31 May 2019
6.1.3 Protection
1 If there is protection securing the instrument, this is captured in the separate
2 protection entity.
3 The protection entity contains the information about all protection items (i.e. valuable
4 assets or rights) that are committed to the fulfilment of the terms of an instrument
5 (i.e. that secure the payments under a credit transaction), as specified in the (credit)
6 contract that gives rise to the instrument. All protection items in the protection entity
7 have an instrument identifier such that the protection item can be linked to the
8 instrument it secures.
9 When defining the data model, the possibility that the same protection item may be
10 associated with several instruments is taken into account. This could imply that a
11 protection item appears in the protection entity multiple times in relation to different
12 instruments. The same protection item would therefore appear in several entries,
13 with the protection entity relating to a different instrument in each information triple
14 (of instrument, protection and counterparty). This nevertheless involves no repetition
15 of the protection information across different instruments (e.g. the allocated amount
16 specific to each instrument).
17 Protection always involves at least one counterparty – the protection provider. The
18 counterparty which grants the protection is identified and reported to AnaCredit (unless
19 it is a natural person). The counterparty is described in the counterparty entity.
20 In the context of AnaCredit, the protection value (and consequently also the allocated
21 protection value) is reported gross of any haircut (i.e. before any haircut is applied).
6.1.4 Counterparty
22 An instrument always involves counterparties. The counterparties are described in
23 the counterparty entity.
24 The counterparty entity contains information about counterparties related to the
25 instrument entity and, if relevant, to the protection entity. The counterparty entity also
26 contains information about certain counterparties affiliated with debtors and
27 protection providers of an instrument in the instrument entity.
28 In a similar way to the modelling of the instrument and protection entities, the
29 modelling of the counterparty entity takes into account the fact that the same
30 counterparty may relate to several instruments and protection items.
31 For the purpose of AnaCredit, all counterparties which take any of the following roles
32 are reflected in the counterparty entity:
33 1. the creditor of the instrument;
34 2. the originator of the instrument, if the instrument is a securitisation
35 transaction;

2 4. the debtor of the instrument;

4 protection item is provided);
5 6. the head office undertaking of (any foreign branch or a special fund19 that is)
6 a debtor of the instrument or a protection provider that provides protection to
7 the instrument;
8 7. the immediate parent undertaking of any debtor of the instrument, or of any
9 protection provider that provides protection to the instrument;
10 8. the ultimate parent undertaking of any debtor of the instrument, or of any
11 protection provider that provides protection to the instrument.
12 On any given date, a counterparty may assume one or more of these roles in relation
13 to one or more instruments. Similarly, a single role may be assumed by many
14 counterparties on any given date.

6.1.5 Conceptual representation – the observed agent’s perspective
18 Revision mark: this paragraph is Given the distinct data entities of a credit and taking the perspective of an observed
adjusted to align with the
19 agent, AnaCredit’s conceptual representation of credit consists of a set of fact
perspective taken in Chart 14
20 schemata that basically model facts, measures, dimensions, and hierarchies21 with
21 reference to credit vis-à-vis the credit institution.
22 The AnaCredit conceptual data model establishes a broad view of what should be
23 considered in the AnaCredit reporting, as the data model includes the distinct data
24 entities and the relationships between them. However, the conceptual data model
25 specifies neither data attributes nor primary keys. Yet, choosing a conceptual data
26 model means that dimensions, measures and the granularity of data have been
27 defined.
19 Please refer to Section 3.1 for details regarding special funds.
20 Reporting agents may use the same counterparty entity for managing the instruments as for
reporting to AnaCredit. In this case, the data on natural persons, although they are part of
counterparty data of the reporting agents, are not reported to AnaCredit.
21 In data modelling theory a “fact” is a concept that models a set of events (e.g. credit held or
serviced by a bank). In essence, a fact has dynamic properties or evolves in some way over
time. A “measure” is a numerical property of a fact and describes a quantitative fact aspect that
is relevant to analysis. For example, every credit is quantified at a given moment in time by its
nominal outstanding amount. A “qualitative dimension” (or data attribute) is a fact property with a
finite “domain” (i.e. a set of potential values) and describes an analysis coordinate of the fact.
The dimensions for the credit fact are type of credit, currency, dates, etc. Finally, “hierarchy”
determines how fact instances may be aggregated and selected, and determines the granularity
adopted for representing facts.

6.2 Logical data model – the reporting agent’s perspective
15 Revision mark: this paragraph is The logical data model contains more details than the AnaCredit conceptual data
enhanced with further clarifications
16 model. In particular, the logical data model:
17 • includes all entity tables (i.e. distinct parts in which the data are grouped on the
18 basis of its nature) and relationships between them;
19 • specifies data attributes (i.e. individual characteristics that describe the facts
20 recorded) for each data entity;
21 • specifies a primary key for each data entity (i.e. one or a combination of
22 identifiers – identifying data attributes – that uniquely identifies a record in a
23 data entity);
24 • specifies foreign keys (i.e. one or combination of identifiers – identifying data
25 attributes – which allow the relationship between different data entities to be
26 identified.
27 The logical data model also involves normalisation, which is the process of removing
28 redundancy in an entity table. Normalisation typically occurs by dividing an entity
29 table into two or more and defining relationships between the tables. Consequently,
22 A many-to-many relationship is a type of cardinality that refers to the relationship between two
entities A and B in which A may contain one record related to several records in B and vice
versa. For instance, an instrument is secured by many protection items and one protection item
secures many instruments.
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 101
31 May 2019
1 the AnaCredit logical data model comprises more explicit data entities than the
2 conceptual data model. This is motivated by the replacement of any many-to-many
3 relationships in the conceptual model with one-to-many relationships23, which is
4 achieved by introducing bridging tables.
5 The AnaCredit logical data model from the reporting agent’s perspective is depicted
6 in Chart 15 (as opposed to Chart 14 above, which shows the observed agent’s
7 perspective). This means that the observed agent is not fixed and is therefore
8 incorporated into the entity relationship diagram.
9 The reference date is fixed in the entity relationship diagram, meaning that all the
10 data therein are valid as of the reference date.
11 The AnaCredit logical data model is presented from the reporting agent’s perspective
12 because of the requirement (Point 1.2 of Annex I of the AnaCredit Regulation) to
13 uniquely identify the counterparty at the level of the reporting agent (see also the
14 definition of the counterparty identifier in Annex IV of the AnaCredit Regulation).
23 A one-to-many relationship exists when one instance in table A may be linked with many
instances in table B, but one instance in table B is linked to only one instance in table A. It is
important to note that a one-to-many relationship is not a property of the data, but rather of the
relationship itself.

Example 26: Counterparty identifier unique for the reporting agent
The reporting agent RA0 (a credit institution) reports for its two observed agents:
RA0_OA1 (the domestic part of the credit institution) and RA0_OA2 (a foreign branch of
the credit institution).
The observed agent RA0_OA1 holds an instrument in which client C is a debtor. The
observed agent RA0_OA1 uses the counterparty identifier Client_123 to uniquely
identify client C.
Similarly, the observed agent RA0_OA2 holds two instruments in which client C is a
debtor. However, the observed agent RA0_OA2 uses the counterparty identifier
Cpty_9867 to uniquely identify client C.
The reporting agent RA0 recognises that the counterparty identifiers Client_123 used by
the observed agent RA0_OA1 and the counterparty identifier Cpty_9867 used by the
observed agent RA0_OA2 both refer to the same client C.
Subsequently, to comply with the primary key definition of the counterparty reference
data entity table, the reporting agent RA0 assigns a unique counterparty identifier
Client_123_Cpty_9867 to Client C and uses this counterparty identifier to substitute the
different counterparty identifiers used in relation to the same client C in all the respective
entity tables of the two observed agents.
6.2.1.2 Foreign keys for each entity table
1 Foreign keys identify the relationships between the different entities. In particular, a
2 foreign key is one or more identifiers in one entity table that uniquely identifies a row
3 of another entity table. In other words, a foreign key is defined in the second entity
4 table but refers to the primary key in the first table.
5 For example, the combination (observed agent identifier, contract identifier,
6 instrument identifier) is a foreign key in the instrument-protection received entity
7 table that refers to the primary key in the instrument entity table. The combination
8 (observed agent identifier, protection identifier) in the instrument-protection received
9 entity table refers to the primary key in the protection entity table.
10 The foreign keys for each entity table are specified in Chart 15: AnaCredit logical
11 data model – the reporting agent’s perspective at the beginning of Section 6.2 (and
12 in Chart 16: AnaCredit logical data model and reportable datasets – the reporting
13 agent’s perspective in Section 6.3), where they are abbreviated as FK in the
14 respective entity tables.
6.2.2 Entity tables of the logical data model
15 The logical data model specifies data attributes for each entity table. A data attribute
16 is an individual characteristic to be collected and registered in a given entity table
17 (field/column).
18 Revision mark: editorial The data entity tables as referred to in the logical data model differ from the actual
adjustments are made to this
19 AnaCredit reportable datasets. The difference arises when certain data attributes of

AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 107
31 May 2019
1 a data entity are required for different frequencies or reporting methods (for example,
2 some data attributes are reported monthly, while others are reported quarterly).
3 Please refer to section 6.3 for more details. To achieve a high level of consistency
4 and data quality, all the data attributes are required to be compiled taking the
5 following principles into account:
6 • all the data attributes are valid as of the same date.
7 On any given reference date, a data attribute represents a specific feature that is
8 valid or regarded as valid as of that reference date. All data attributes are valid as of
9 the same reference date – i.e. they represent specific features at the same moment
10 in time.
11 • all the data attributes of the same table are defined on the same level of
12 granularity.
13 All data attributes in the same entity table relate to the same element and are
14 defined on the same level of granularity (i.e. the level corresponding to a single row
15 in a given entity table).
16 The data attributes to be compiled and collected in each entity table are listed below.
17 The definitions of the fields are provided in Part II of this Manual.
6.2.2.1 The instrument entity table
6.2.2.1.1 Definition of the instrument entity table
18 The instrument entity table is the centrepiece of the data model. This means that all
19 other entity tables relate directly or indirectly to the instrument entity table. The
20 instrument entity table collects specific information that describes the instrument,
21 such as the basic features of the instrument, the financial aspects of the instrument
22 and the accounting features of the instrument.
6.2.2.1.2 Description
23 The data in the instrument entity table describe both features of the instrument which
24 change rarely over time and features which reflect the instrument’s financial
25 development in accordance with the relevant accounting standard. Such features are
26 captured via respective data attributes which are required to describe the instrument
27 as of the same reference date. This means that any information collected is accurate
28 as of a given reference date. Any relevant dependencies between the data attributes
29 are also reflected accordingly.
30 Example 27 provides a representation of certain features of an instrument (a loan)
31 over time, with a focus on the relationship between the features.
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 108
31 May 2019
Example 27: Selected information in the instrument entity table
A loan (credit) is represented by an instrument. The outstanding amount of the loan is
€10,000.
The instrument becomes non-performing as of 16 September. As of 20 October, the
loan is fully provisioned (i.e. an impairment loss is recognised), and as of 26 November
the loan is written-off.
The following table provides an overview of the selected features of the instrument and
how they evolve over time, taking into account the mutual dependencies between the
features, and following the events prescribed (leaving aside the fact that the data
attributes “accumulated impairment amount”, “performing status of the instrument” and
“accumulated write-offs” are not required for non-quarter-end dates).
Outstanding Accumulated
Instrument nominal impairment Performing status Accumulated
Date ID amount amount of the instrument write-offs
31/08/2019 Instrument 1 10,000.00 0.00 Performing 0.00
30/09/2019 Instrument 1 10,000.00 0.00 Non-performing 0.00
31/10/2019 Instrument 1 10,000.00 10,000.00 Non-performing 0.00
30/11/2019 Instrument 1 0.00 0.00 Non-performing 10,000.00
Notably, the write-off in November results in:
• the outstanding nominal amount being reduced to €0, as following the accounting
rules the write-off leads to the derecognition of the loan from the balance sheet;
• the accumulated impairment amount being reduced to €0, as this amount
corresponds exactly to the outstanding debt of the loan.
Please note that this example only illustrates the logic within the instrument entity table.
It does not indicate what and at which point in time is actually reported to AnaCredit.

Example 28: Relationships between counterparties and instruments
One counterparty may act as both creditor and servicer, while a different counterparty
acts as debtor. In this case, there are still three records (for the creditor, servicer and
debtor) in the counterparty-instrument entity table, all linked to the same instrument.
Conversely, several different counterparties may be linked with a single instrument if
there are, for instance, several debtors in relation to a single instrument. Each of these
relationships requires a separate record in the counterparty-instrument entity table.

2 the instrument-protection received entity table (one record for each protection
3 item securing the instrument).

5 record in the instrument entity table.
Example 29: Relationships between instruments and protection
If an instrument is unsecured, there is no record for this instrument in the instrument-
protection received entity table.
Conversely, if an instrument is secured by several different protection items, there are
as many records for this instrument in the instrument-protection received entity table as
there are protection items securing the instrument.

6.2.2.2 The counterparty-instrument entity table
6.2.2.2.1 Definition of the counterparty-instrument entity table
4 The counterparty-instrument entity table is the set of all combinations of instruments
5 reported pursuant to Articles 4 and 5 within the scope of the reporting agent and
6 related counterparties which assume any of the roles of creditor, servicer, debtor
7 and, if applicable, originator vis-à-vis the instrument.
6.2.2.2.2 Description
8 The relationships between counterparties to the instrument are registered in the
9 counterparty-instrument entity table, which includes the counterparties directly
10 involved in the instrument and their respective roles vis-à-vis the instrument.
11 Specifically, the entity table registers all (non-natural person) counterparties which
12 take the role of:
13 • debtor of the instrument;
14 • creditor of the instrument;
15 • servicer of the instrument.
16 Under certain circumstances, registration also includes counterparties which take the
17 role of:
18 • originator to the instrument (if the instrument is a securitisation transaction)

21 the counterparty-instrument entity table whose counterparty role is debtor.

Example 30: Instrument granted to a legal entity and a natural person (partial
liability)
As of 30 September, the reporting agent RA_1 reports data of the observed agent
RA1_OA1 following the logical data model.
The counterparty Legal entity A and the counterparty Natural person are both partially
liable for the instrument Instrument_A_1 registered in the instrument entity table. Both
counterparties are partially (and equally) liable for making repayments of
Instrument_A_1, i.e. each of them is liable for 50% of the instrument. The outstanding
nominal amount registered in the instrument entity table is €100,000. The partial liability
of each counterparty is 50%.

counterparty-instrument entity with its role as debtor and the corresponding liability
amount of €50,000.

counterparty-instrument entity table.

6.2.2.2.3 Record
3 For any instrument identified and registered in the instrument entity table, there are
4 as many records in the counterparty-instrument entity table as there are
5 counterparties assuming any of the roles of creditor, debtor, servicer or originator of
6 that instrument, double- (or triple-) counting any counterparties that assume two (or
7 more) roles (i.e. if a counterparty acts as both creditor and servicer, there are still two
8 records relating to this counterparty in the counterparty-instrument entity table) but
9 excluding all counterparties that are natural persons.
10 Conversely, the counterparty-instrument entity table comprises records of those
11 counterparties which a) assume any of the roles of creditor, servicer, debtor and the
12 originator in relation to any reported instrument and b) are not natural persons,
13 taking into account the requirement that a counterparty cannot appear multiple times
14 in the same role in relation to one instrument.
25 Note that the counterparty risk/default entity table comprises also counterparties other than
debtors, cf. section 6.2.2.5.

Example 32: Relationships between counterparties to instruments and the
counterparty entity
A counterparty which acts as both creditor and servicer of the same instrument is
recorded in the counterparty-instrument entity table in two different records. This means
that two records also link with this counterparty in the counterparty reference data entity
table.
A counterparty (a protection provider) may grant protection securing an instrument
without assuming any of the roles of creditor, servicer, debtor or originator in relation to
the instrument. In this case, the protection provider is not reported in the counterparty-
instrument entity table. However, every protection provider which is not a natural person
is registered in the counterparty reference data entity table.
23 There is a relationship between the counterparty-instrument entity table and the
24 instrument entity table:
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 116
31 May 2019
1 • One record in the counterparty-instrument entity table links with exactly one
2 record in the instrument entity table.
3 • One record in the instrument entity table links with as many records in the
4 counterparty-instrument table as there are counterparties assuming any of the
5 roles of debtor, creditor, servicer, or originator to this instrument, double- (or
6 triple-) counting counterparties that assume multiple roles (e.g., creditor and
7 servicer) but excluding all counterparties that are natural persons. There are a
8 minimum of three records in the counterparty-instrument entity table for every
9 instrument detailing its relationships with creditor, servicer and debtor, none of
10 which may be a natural person. Please note that if all debtors are natural
11 persons the instrument is not subject to reporting requirements pursuant to
12 Articles 4 and 5 of the AnaCredit Regulation.
Example 33: Relationships between counterparties to instruments and instruments
If one instrument links with no more than two counterparties (one assuming the roles of
creditor and servicer, the other assuming the role of debtor), then there are three
different records in the counterparty-instrument entity table.
Conversely, there may be many debtors (other than natural persons) of a single
instrument, each of them requiring a separate record in the counterparty-instrument
entity table. The total number of possible records in the counterparty-instrument entity
table relating to a single instrument is thus driven by the number of different
counterparties involved in the instrument in any of the following roles: creditor, servicer,
debtor or originator.
13 The following example illustrates the above set of relationships between instruments
14 and counterparties.
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 117
31 May 2019
Example 34: Relationships between the counterparty and the instrument
For a given credit, represented by an instrument, there is always at least one debtor of
the instrument. The debtor is registered in the counterparty-instrument entity table and
is associated with the debtor counterparty role therein.
Any counterparty (other than a natural person) registered in the counterparty-instrument
entity table is registered in the counterparty reference data entity table. In particular, for
any debtor of an instrument the relevant debtor information (name, address, etc.) is
registered in the counterparty reference data entity table.
In the case of natural persons involved in instruments, for AnaCredit purposes, no entry
is made in the counterparty-instrument entity table and consequently no record appears
in the counterparty reference data entity table.
A number of distinct counterparties registered in the counterparty reference data entity
table may be debtors of several distinct instruments or just one instrument (i.e. in the
case of joint debtors) registered in the instrument entity table.
If an instrument relates to multiple (non-natural person) debtors then this instrument is
registered in the counterparty-instrument entity table multiple times. There is therefore a
repetition of the instrument identifier and other instrument information in multiple
separate entries with different debtor identifiers.
Some counterparties registered in the counterparty reference data entity table may not
be directly linked with any instrument registered in the instrument entity table.
Specifically, a counterparty that is a protection provider (e.g. a guarantor) is not linked to
any instrument in the counterparty-instrument entity table. Similarly, the head office
undertaking of a counterparty that is a debtor of an instrument may not be directly linked
to any instrument in the instrument entity table. Therefore, no such counterparty is
registered in the counterparty-instrument entity table.

6.2.2.3 The instrument-protection received entity table
6.2.2.3.1 Definition of the instrument-protection received entity table
4 The instrument-protection received entity table is the set of all combinations of
5 instruments reported pursuant to Articles 4 and 5 of the AnaCredit Regulation within
6 the scope of the reporting agent and the related protection items which secure the
7 instrument. It follows that, while all protection items in the protection received entity
8 table secure at least one instrument in the instrument entity table and hence appear
9 in the instrument-protection received entity table, instruments which are unsecured
10 do not appear in the instrument-protection received entity table.

12 received entity table, along with data on the extent to which the given protection item
13 secures the instrument.

4 Please note that the level of granularity does not include the protection provider

7 provided by several protection providers (for example, joint guarantors providing a
8 financial guarantee). Special treatment is therefore required if there are several
9 protection providers for the same protection item.
10 Specifically, although reporting agents identify all protection providers of any
11 protection item in their systems (e.g. by maintaining a relationship table between
12 protection items and their protection providers in line with the
13 counterparty-instrument dataset), only one of several protection providers is
14 technically reported to AnaCredit. The AnaCredit Regulation does not specify any
15 particular requirements as to which of the several protection providers is actually to
16 be reported.

6.2.2.5 The counterparty risk/default entity table
6.2.2.5.1 Definition of the counterparty risk/default entity table
3 The counterparty risk/default entity table is the set of all counterparties which are
4 debtors of any instrument reported pursuant to Articles 4 and 5 of the AnaCredit
5 Regulation within the scope of the reporting agent, with multiple counting of any
6 counterparty that is a debtor of instruments which relate to multiple observed agents.
7 The counterparty risk/default entity table also contains those counterparties (other
8 than natural persons) that provide protection in the form of financial guarantees (cf.
9 Section 6.2.2.4.2 for details) as registered in the protection received entity table.
6.2.2.5.2 Description
10 The counterparty risk/default entity table provides information on the probability of
11 default of the counterparty, the default status of the counterparty and the date of the
12 default status of the counterparty.

Example 39: Relationships between counterparty reference data and counterparty
risk/default
If a counterparty in the counterparty reference data entity table does not act as debtor
or provider (and issuer) of protection in the form of unfunded credit protection as defined
in Article 4(1)(59) of the CRR (such as a financial guarantee, cf. Section 6.2.2.4.2) in
relation to any instrument of the observed agent reported under AnaCredit, this
counterparty does not link to any record in the counterparty risk/default entity table.
If a counterparty in the counterparty reference data entity table acts as debtor in the
counterparty-instrument dataset to several instruments that relate to the same observed
agent, the counterparty is reported only once in the counterparty risk/default entity table.
If a counterparty in the counterparty reference data entity table acts as debtor or
provider (and issuer) of unfunded protection to several instruments held by different
observed agents within the scope of the same reporting agent, then the counterparty is
reported in the counterparty risk/default entity table relating to each of the observed
agents which hold any instrument in relation to which this counterparty is a debtor or for
which the counterparty provides a financial guarantee. In particular, the PD and default
status of the counterparty that are reported in relation to this counterparty are identical
across different observed agents of one reporting agent.
For counterparties registered in the counterparty risk/default entity table, relevant
counterparty information is registered in the counterparty reference data entity table.
Immediate and ultimate parent undertakings of a debtor (or a protection provider which
is also the protection issuer) of an instrument are also registered in the counterparty
reference data entity table. However, immediate and ultimate parent undertakings do
not need to be debtors of any instrument registered in the instrument entity table or
protection providers. Immediate and ultimate parent undertakings thus do not need to
be registered in the counterparty risk/default entity table.

6.2.2.6 The counterparty reference data entity table
6.2.2.6.1 Definition of the counterparty reference data entity table
7 The counterparty reference data entity table is the set of all institutional units which
8 are linked to instruments reported pursuant to Articles 4 and Article 5 of the
9 AnaCredit Regulation or provide protection to secure such, or are affiliated with
10 debtors or protection providers (AnaCredit Regulation, Annex I, Template 1, 1.3).
11 Each counterparty registered in the counterparty reference data entity table is
12 uniquely identified at the level of the observed agent’s legal entity (the credit
13 institution). This requirement is discussed in more detail in Section 3.1. No data on
14 natural persons are required in the counterparty reference data entity table.
6.2.2.6.2 Description
Specifically, the counterparties to be registered are:
(a) creditors;
(b) debtors;
(c) protection providers;
(d) originators;

(e) servicers;

(h) ultimate parent undertakings.

6.3 Reportable datasets and reporting timeliness
3 The actual datasets to be reported are derived from the entity tables of the AnaCredit
4 logical data model, taking into consideration different methods for reporting the data
5 to AnaCredit and various reporting frequencies.
6.3.1 Reportable datasets
6 On a general level, AnaCredit requires that reporting agents report granular credit,
7 protection and counterparty information on a regular basis. More specifically, three
8 types of reporting frequencies have been introduced in the AnaCredit Regulation:
9 monthly, quarterly and on change.

6.3.2 Reporting methods, frequencies and timeliness
3 In general, AnaCredit anticipates that all data describe a credit (i.e., instrument,

5 the reporting reference date). However, AnaCredit provides for different reporting
6 methods and frequencies for different datasets.
7 AnaCredit distinguishes between two different reporting methods:
(a) regular, where all records are reported;
(b) on change, where only new or changed records are reported.
8 AnaCredit distinguishes between two different reporting frequencies: (i) monthly
9 frequency and (ii) quarterly frequency.

31 May 2019
1 Please note that a new record covers the situation where a new instrument is
2 originated by the observed agent or a protection item is added in the period between
3 two consecutive reporting reference dates.
4 Quarterly reporting, meanwhile, means that the respective records of a dataset (i.e.
5 all records) are submitted to AnaCredit every quarter pursuant to the timelines
6 relevant for reporting data relating to an observed agent.
7 Different timeliness applies for submission of datasets (all records including
8 new/changed records) depending on the residency status of the observed agent.
9 In particular, for resident observed agents:
10 • data reported monthly under Article 13(4) of the AnaCredit Regulation are
11 reported by NCBs to the ECB within 30 working days of the reporting reference
12 date (end of month) to which they refer;
13 • data reported quarterly under Article 13(5) of the AnaCredit Regulation are
14 reported by NCBs to the ECB within 15 working days of the remittance date
15 (defined in Article 3(1)(b) of Commission Implementing Regulation (EU) No
16 680/2014 – hereinafter referred to as “the ITS”) following the reporting reference
17 date (end of month) to which they refer.
Revision mark: an explanation is
18 added regarding non-resident For non-resident observed agents (i.e. observed agents that are foreign branches
19 foreign branches not resident in a reporting Member State), the following timelines applies:
20 • data reported monthly under Article 13(6) of the AnaCredit Regulation are
21 reported by NCBs to the ECB within 35 working days of the reporting reference
22 date (end of month) to which they refer;
23 • data reported quarterly under Article 13(7) of the AnaCredit Regulation are
24 reported by NCBs to the ECB within 20 working days of the remittance date
25 (defined in Article 3(1)(b) of the ITS) following the reporting reference date (end
26 of month) to which they refer.
27 The exact timeliness depends on the number of ECB and NCBs public holidays in
28 the reference period concerned.
29 The counterparty reference data dataset is compiled at reporting agent level
30 (counterparties contained therein are unique at the level of the reporting agent) and
31 the specific timelines for observed agents do not generally apply. More specifically, if
32 the reporting agent reports the activity as creditor or servicer of both resident and
33 non-resident observed agents, the different timelines are aligned to ensure
34 uniqueness of the counterparty reference data at the reporting agent level. Any
35 changes in the counterparty reference data therefore are reported following the
36 timelines envisaged for resident observed agents.

Reporting all records means that the complete dataset (new, changed and unchanged
records) is sent monthly or quarterly to AnaCredit (as indicated in the “When to report”
column).
Reporting only new or changed means reporting only those records that are either new
records or have been changed (i.e. one or more data attributes of a record have
changed) with the result that the values provided previously are no longer valid.

Example 44: Reporting in the case of a single change in a data attribute
This example concerns the instrument dataset. A change in one data attribute (e.g.
payment frequency) is acknowledged by the reporting agent on 22 October 2019. This
change relates to an instrument already reported to AnaCredit.
Given this change, a complete record (i.e. all the data attributes in one row, whether
affected or unaffected by the change) of the instrument dataset is reported by no later
than the 30th working day after the earliest reporting reference date on which the
change is in effect.
Since the relevant reference date for the change is 31 October 2019, the record is
reported to AnaCredit within 30 working days of the reporting reference date.

Example 45: Reporting in the case of multiple changes in the same data attribute in
the same month
This example concerns the instrument dataset. A change in one data attribute (e.g.
payment frequency) is acknowledged by the reporting agent on 22 October 2019.
However, on 27 October 2019 the data attribute is changed again. These changes
relate to an instrument already reported to AnaCredit.
Given that only the latter change is in effect on the earliest reporting reference date (i.e.
31 October 2019), the former change (on 22 October 2019) is irrelevant and only the
change on 27 October is reported.
A complete record of the instrument dataset is reported to AnaCredit within 30 working
days of 31 October 2019.

Example 46: Reporting in the case of multiple changes in different data attributes
and dates in the same month
This example concerns the instrument dataset. A change in one data attribute (e.g.
payment frequency) is acknowledged by the reporting agent on 22 October 2019. On 27
October 2019 a change is made in another data attribute of the instrument dataset (e.g.
repayment rights). These changes relate to an instrument already reported to
AnaCredit.
Since both changes are in effect as of 31 October 2019, the timeline for reporting both
changes is 30 working days after 31 October 2019.
A single complete record (i.e. all the data attributes in one row, whether affected and
unaffected by the change) of the instrument dataset is submitted to update the two data
attributes changed.

Example 47: Reporting in the case of multiple changes in consecutive months
This example concerns the instrument dataset. A change in one data attribute of the
data (e.g. payment frequency) is acknowledged by the reporting agent on 22 October
2019. This data attribute is changed again on 3 November 2019. These changes relate
to an instrument already reported to AnaCredit.
Given that only the former change is in effect on the earliest reporting reference date
(i.e. 31 October 2019), while the latter change (on 3 November 2019) is only in effect on
30 November, the reporting timelines are as follows:
• The first change (on 22 October 2019) is reported within 30 working days of 31
October 2019.
• The second change (on 3 November 2019) is reported within 30 working days of 30
November 2019.
This means that a complete record (i.e. all the data attributes in one row) of the
instrument dataset is reported to AnaCredit within 30 working days of 31 October 2019
(for the change on 22 October 2019).
Another complete record of the instrument dataset is reported to AnaCredit within 30
working days of 30 November 2019 (for the change on 3 November 2019)

7 Article 7 and reduced data requirements
1 Pursuant to Article 6(1) of the AnaCredit Regulation, reporting agents report to
2 AnaCredit all data attributes listed in the templates in Annex I of the AnaCredit
3 Regulation.
4 Reduced data requirements under However, as stipulated in Article 7, the reporting requirements may be reduced in
Annexes II and III
5 certain specific cases. These cases are described in Annex II and III of the
6 AnaCredit Regulation.
7 In fact, the AnaCredit Regulation distinguishes between:
8 • specific cases in relation to counterparty reference data;
9 • specific cases in relation to the remaining data attributes.
10 Annex III deals with reduced requirements for counterparty reference data, while
11 Annex II outlines reduced requirements for the remaining datasets.
12 In other words, the AnaCredit Regulation essentially requires that whenever an
13 instrument is reported to AnaCredit, reporting agents submit all the data attributes
14 listed in Annex I thereof. However, exemptions may apply in relation to certain data
15 attributes and under certain conditions.
16 General exemptions versus national Accordingly, the AnaCredit Regulation contains a classification of the specific
exemptions
17 circumstances under which a certain data attribute may not be required. A distinction
18 is made between the following:
(a) circumstances under which individual reporting agents may be exempted
from reporting certain data attributes by the relevant NCB;
(b) circumstances under which reporting agents are not required to report
certain data attributes at all.
19 Specific data attributes whose collection is at NCBs’ discretion (case (a) above) are
20 marked as “N” in Annex II and Annex III of the AnaCredit Regulation. Data attributes
21 that are not required to be reported (case (b) above) are marked as “X” in Annex II
22 and Annex III of the AnaCredit Regulation.
23 Required versus not required All data attributes that are not marked as either “N” or “X” in Annex II or Annex III of
24 the AnaCredit Regulation are required to be reported, in other words reporting
25 agents are obliged to report the actual value for such data attributes as of the
26 reporting reference date, where the actual value provides information about the
27 respective feature as of the reporting reference date to which it refers.
28 Revision mark: a reference to For information regarding the reporting of data attributes which are not (or may not
Section 2.2 in Part II of the Manual
29 be, at NCBs’ discretion) required or which do not apply under certain circumstances,
is added regarding special reporting
30 values please refer to Section 2.2 in Part II of the Manual which deals specifically with
31 special reporting values.

7.1 General rules regarding data attributes marked as “X”
1 “X” data attributes are not Under the specified circumstances, the collection of any data attribute marked as “X”
mandatory
2 in Annex II or Annex III is not mandatory.
3 This means that reporting agents are not required to report the actual value for these
4 data attributes to AnaCredit in the specified situation.
5 The exemption from reporting certain data attributes to AnaCredit is nevertheless
6 without prejudice to national requirements. As NCBs may, on the basis of national
7 regulations, extend reporting obligations beyond the scope defined in the AnaCredit
8 Regulation, reporting agents in a given country may in fact be required to report
9 some or all of the data attributes marked as “X”. Such data attributes are also
10 transmitted to AnaCredit.
11 If reporting agents choose to report the data attributes not required by the AnaCredit
12 Regulation (i.e. they report the actual values for these data attributes), they are
13 collected by NCBs and transmitted to AnaCredit and are subject to the minimum
14 standards for transmission, accuracy, compliance with concepts and revisions
15 specified in Annex V of the AnaCredit Regulation.
7.2 General rules regarding data attributes marked as “N”
16 “N” data attributes are mandatory Under the specified circumstances, the collection of any data attribute marked as “N”
unless indicated otherwise by the
17 in Annex II or Annex III is mandatory unless decided otherwise by the relevant NCB.
relevant NCB
18 More specifically, NCBs have the right to exempt reporting agents from reporting
19 certain data attributes to AnaCredit under certain specified circumstances.
20 This means that if special conditions apply, the relevant NCB may decide not to
21 require reporting agents to report certain data attributes. Effectively, the reporting of
22 such data attributes is not mandatory under the specified circumstances and
23 reporting agents do not have to report the actual value for these data attributes.
24 Although the specific right of NCBs is deemed to be primarily applicable to individual
25 (or groups of) reporting agents (in cases where a given reporting agent temporarily
26 faces difficulties in obtaining the data), it may also be applied to the reporting
27 population as a whole if the relevant NCB considers that these difficulties exist
28 generally.

3 Registering a counterparty in the counterparty reference data means that a certain

12 In fact, the AnaCredit Regulation stipulates that if a counterparty to be registered in
13 the counterparty reference data is covered by more than one description in Table 2
14 or 3, the most onerous reporting requirement across the descriptions applies in
15 relation to the counterparty for a given data attribute.
16 The most onerous requirement is understood as follows: if a counterparty takes on
17 two roles (e.g. acts as both creditor and servicer) and the same data attribute is
18 required for the one role but not required for the other, the most onerous requirement
19 implies that the data attribute is required for the counterparty.
20 Example 48 illustrates how to determine whether a data attribute is reported to
21 AnaCredit in the event that a counterparty takes on more than one role listed in the
22 headers of Table 2 (and Table 3) in Annex III to the AnaCredit Regulation.
Example 48: Most onerous requirement takes precedence
Assumptions:
• In relation to the reporting reference date 31 March 2019 the instrument INS_1 of
the observed agent RA_1_OA_1 is reported to AnaCredit by the reporting agent
RA_1. The counterparty Ctpy_A is a debtor of the instrument INS_1. The
instrument originates after 1 September 2018.
• In relation to the same reporting reference date, the reporting agent RA_1 reports
to AnaCredit the instrument INS_2 of the observed agent RA_1_OA_1. The
counterparty Ctpy_A is a protection provider for the instrument.
• The counterparty Ctpy_A is resident in a reporting Member State. The counterparty
is a legal entity. The reporting agent RA_1 reports no other instruments in which
the counterparty Ctpy_A is involved and the counterparty is not affiliated with any
other debtor or protection provider reported by the reporting agent RA_1.
Which data attributes are required for the counterparty Ctpy_A in the counterparty
reference data?
In relation to the data reported by the reporting agent RA_1, the counterparty Ctpy_A
takes on only two roles:
• debtor — at least one instrument originated on or after 1 September 2018;
• protection provider.
AnaCredit Reporting Manual – Part I – General methodology 146
31 May 2019
However, the counterparty only is registered in the counterparty reference data once.
The counterparty is uniquely identified by its counterparty identifier and the data
attributes to be registered are determined as follows:
In accordance with Table 2 (counterparty resident in a resident Member State), the
economic activity is required for the debtor’s role but may not be required for the
protection provider’s role depending on the decision of the relevant NCB. Since the
most onerous requirement takes precedence, the economic activity is required for the
counterparty Ctpy_A regardless of the NCB’s decision regarding the requirement for
protection providers.
Repeating the reasoning for all data attributes, the counterparty reference data reported
by the reporting agent RA_1 in relation to the counterparty Ctpy_A ultimately contains at
least the following data attributes:
• counterparty identifier (always required);
• national identifier;
• head office undertaking identifier;
• immediate parent undertaking identifier;
• ultimate parent undertaking identifier;
• name;
• address: street;
• address: city/town/village;
• address: county/administrative division;
• address: postal code;
• address: country;
• legal form;
• institutional sector;
• economic activity;
• status of legal proceedings;
• date of initiation of legal proceedings;
• enterprise size;
• date of enterprise size;
• number of employees;
• balance sheet total;
• annual turnover;
These data attributes are generally required in relation to the counterparty Ctpy_A
because they are required by the AnaCredit Regulation for debtors with at least one
instrument originated at or after 1 September 2018 (and thus required) or are required
for both debtors and protection providers.
The only data attribute that is not required in relation to the counterparty is the
accounting standard, as this attribute is only required for reporting agents and the
counterparty in question is not the reporting agent reporting the instrument.
With regard to the legal entity identifier (LEI), this data attribute may not be required for
the counterparty concerned depending on what the relevant NCB decides.

Example 49: More stringent requirements on subsequent reporting reference dates
The counterparty Ctpy_B is a servicer of an instrument of the observed agent
RA_1_OA_1 reported by the reporting agent RA_1 as of a given reporting reference
date. The counterparty Ctpy_B does not take on any other role in relation to any
instruments reported by the reporting agent RA_1.
The set of attributes to be reported in relation to the counterparty Ctpy_B is that which is
required for servicers resident in a reporting Member State as set out in Table 2
(column 11) of Annex III of the AnaCredit Regulation.
However, if on a subsequent reporting reference date the reporting agent reports an
additional instrument of which the counterparty Ctpy_B is a debtor, then the reporting
agent updates the counterparty reference data accordingly to account for the fact that
the counterparty Ctpy_B takes on two roles (servicer and debtor) as of the subsequent
reporting reference date. Again, the most onerous requirement across these roles takes
precedence (in this case, it is the role of debtor).
6 By contrast, in the opposite case where fewer data attributes are required for a
7 counterparty from one period to the next it is not necessary to update the
8 counterparty reference data by removing data attributes that are no longer strictly
9 required, provided such data remains up to date.

Example 50: Determining the least onerous requirement
Data of the observed agent RA_1_OA_1 are reported by the reporting agent RA_1. The
observed agent RA_1_OA_1 is neither resident in a reporting Member State nor is
subject to capital requirements under the CRR.
The observed agent holds the instrument INST_1, which originated before 1 September
2018. The instrument is recognised and is secured by the protection item
PROT_1_INST_1. Please note that no additional instrument of the observed agent that
originated on or after 1 September 2018 is secured by the same protection item
PROT_1_INST_1. The counterparty Cpty_D is the debtor of the instrument.
In accordance with Table 1 of Annex II of the AnaCredit Regulation, the corresponding
reporting requirements are summarised below. The conditions to be verified are 1, 2 and
4. Specifically, the data attributes highlighted in orange in the last column (least onerous
requirement) are required unless the relevant NCB considers that they are not required
to be reported. The data attribute “prudential portfolio” is not required. All other data
attributes, including those not listed in the table, are required to be reported to
AnaCredit.
Please note that in Table 4 below, the data attributes that are subject to reduced
requirements depending on the applicability of the four cases have been highlighted in
different colours:
• data attributes that may be exempted from reporting at NCBs’ discretion are
highlighted in orange;
• data attributes that are not required are highlighted in green.
In addition, grey denotes those cases which are not applicable in the given situation,
while all other cells (in white) indicate that no special treatment applies.

7.4.1 Observed agents that are not resident in a reporting Member State
5 With regard to Case 1 as referred to in Annex II of the AnaCredit Regulation, in
6 accordance with Article 6(2) data of observed agents both resident and non-resident
7 in a reporting Member State are generally subject to AnaCredit reporting. This
8 means that reporting agents which comprise several institutional units (the domestic
9 part and any foreign branches) are responsible for reporting data relating to all these
10 institutional units.
11 Pursuant to Article 6(4), the However, the AnaCredit Regulation provides that the relevant NCB may either
relevant NCB may decide not to

collect information with regard to
13 non-resident foreign branches Article 6(4), or (b) limit the scope of the collection from non-resident observed agents
14 by not collecting data attributes marked as “N” in Table 1 of Annex II under Case 1,
15 pursuant to Article 7.
16 In both cases, non-resident observed agents are those institutional units of reporting
17 agents which are not located in a reporting Member State. These can only be foreign
18 branches located in a country which is not a reporting Member State.
19 In line with Article 1(1), and as explained in Chapter 2, a reporting Member State
20 means either:
21 • a European Union Member State whose currency is the euro;
22 • a Member State of the European Union whose currency is not the euro that
23 joins AnaCredit on a voluntary basis.
24 Consequently, all observed agents which are not located in a reporting Member
25 State are considered to be non-resident observed agents.
26 Conversely, no observed agent for which the data attribute “address: country” in the
27 counterparty reference data is reported as a reporting Member State fulfils the
28 condition “observed agents that are not resident in a reporting Member State”.
7.4.2 Observed agents not subject to capital requirements
29 Under Case 2, instruments may be subject to less stringent requirements provided
30 that the observed agent whose activity as creditor or servicer is reported:
(a) is not (a legally dependent part of) a credit institution subject to the CRR;
(b) is a foreign branch of a credit institution not subject to the CRR.

1 As explained above, the applicability of this condition can be sufficiently verified at
2 the level of the observed agent without considering individual instruments.
3 The CRR only applies to credit institutions; no foreign branches of credit institutions
4 are covered by this Regulation. Please note that foreign branches (or any branch
5 offices in general) are not directly subject to the CRR or to the CRD IV because a
6 (foreign) branch is a legally dependent part of a legal entity and thus may not be
7 addressed by the CRR directly. Please note also that if a credit institution does not
8 have any foreign branches, its (only) observed agent (i.e., the domestic part) is the
9 credit institution itself.
10 Effectively, given the reporting population and the reference population as defined in
11 the AnaCredit Regulation, all observed agents are legally dependent parts of credit
12 institutions and the only applications of Case 2 are thus (a) in the case of a foreign
13 branch resident in a reporting Member State of a credit institution that is resident
14 outside the European Union and (b) in the case of credit institutions (as defined in
15 the CRR) which are exempt from supervision under Article 2(5) of the CRD IV.

19 the data attribute “balance sheet recognition” takes the value “entirely derecognised”.

7.4.4 Instruments originating prior to 1 September 2018
3 An instrument qualifies as an instrument originating prior to 1 September 2018 if the
4 inception date reported for the instrument in the data attribute “inception date” is
5 before 1 September 2018. Conversely, instruments for which the inception date
6 reported to AnaCredit is on or after 1 September 2018 do not meet the condition
7 “instruments originating prior to 1 September 2018”.
8 Contract changes do not lead to a The application of the condition relies by and large on the inception date of an
change in the inception date
9 instrument (cf. Section 3.4.4 in Part II of the Manual). It should be made clear,
10 therefore, that a modification in the conditions of an (existing) instrument triggers a
11 renegotiation (or forbearance); the inception date of the instrument is not changed. In
12 other words, unless the old contract is cancelled and a new one issued instead,
13 contract changes do not lead to a change in the inception date – changes in the
14 contract are flagged in the respective data attributes and the date of their occurrence
15 is captured by the data attribute “date of status of forbearance and renegotiation”.
16 Identification of renegotiated and Please note that AnaCredit distinguishes between renegotiation and forbearance. In
forborne instruments is flagged via
17 both cases there is an agreement between the creditor and the debtor to amend
the data attribute “status of
18 forbearance and renegotiation” terms and conditions of the original contract, but renegotiation refers only to changes
19 under normal market conditions.
20 A renegotiation is triggered whenever the financial conditions of the instrument are
21 contractually changed. A change qualifies as a contractual change in financial
22 conditions whenever the parties involved agree, in legally binding terms, that the
23 payments and risks born in relation to the instrument change (cf. Section 5.4.12 in
24 Part II of the Manual, which deals specifically with the status of forbearance and
25 renegotiation).
26 Consequently, extending the legal final maturity date of an instrument triggers a
27 renegotiation (or forbearance) but does not trigger a change in the instrument’s
28 inception date.

8 Derogations and reduced reporting
frequency for small reporting agents
1 Reporting agents are in principle subject to the full reporting requirements set out in
2 the Annex I of the AnaCredit Regulation, which specify the minimum requirements
3 that reporting agents should meet to satisfy the ECB’s reporting requirements for
4 AnaCredit.
5 However, to ensure the proportionality of the reporting obligations established in the
6 AnaCredit Regulation, there is scope for NCBs to exempt – or partially exempt –
7 certain reporting agents from these obligations.
8 In particular, the AnaCredit Regulation distinguishes between (i) small reporting
9 agents to whom derogations may be applicable pursuant to Article 16(1) and (ii)
10 small reporting agents that may temporarily report on a quarterly basis pursuant to
11 Article 16(2).
12 In the case of small reporting agents subject to derogations, the relevant NCB will
13 determine (a) the reporting agents to which derogations apply and (b) the
14 requirements that the reporting agents should meet to satisfy the ECB’s reporting
15 requirements for AnaCredit.
16 With regard to small reporting agents exempt from the monthly reporting, the
17 relevant NCB will determine which reporting agents are allowed to report on a
18 quarterly instead of a monthly basis for a fixed period of time until 1 January 2021.

23 basis pursuant to Article 16(2) are in principle subject to the full reporting

6 of loans reported pursuant to the BSI Regulation by such reporting agents does not

Example 51: When to report – timeliness for small reporting agents exempted from
monthly reporting
A reporting agent is exempted by the relevant NCB from reporting on a monthly basis.
This example concerns the instrument dataset.
On 3 January 2019 a new instrument is issued by a resident observed agent whose
data is reported by the reporting agent. The instrument exists as of the end of January,
February and March, and also thereafter.
In line with the exemption from reporting data on a monthly basis, the instrument need
not be reported as of 31 January and 28 February, so the reporting agent is obliged to
report the instrument for the first time as of the end of March. The timeline for reporting
the instrument to AnaCredit is within 30 working days after 31 March 2019.

and eligible for reporting after 31/03/2019
31/01/2019 28/02/2019
No data required No data required
to be reported to be reported
Please note that in addition to the instrument dataset, the reporting agent is also obliged
to submit the other datasets (timeliness: within 30 working days after 31 March 2019
apart from the accounting dataset for which a timeline of 15 working days of the
corresponding ITS remittance date applies).
Returning to the instrument dataset, a change in one data attribute is acknowledged by
the observed/reporting agent on 22 April 2019. This change relates to an instrument
already reported to AnaCredit.
Although the change is actually already in effect as of 30 April 2019, the reporting agent
is only required to update the data as of the end of June 2019 as this is the earliest
reporting reference date for which the reporting agent is required to report. The timeline
for reporting the change in the instrument dataset is within 30 working days after 30
June 2019.

Example 52: Reference period for quarter-end reporting reference dates relevant
for small reporting agents reporting on a quarterly basis
This example looks at how to establish the reporting obligation concerning instruments
that incur a write-off in the case of small reporting agents reporting on a quarterly
instead of a monthly basis:
• An instrument is fully written-off as of 15 September 2018. In this case, the
reporting agent still reports the instrument for reporting reference date 30
September 2018.
• An instrument is fully written-off as of 22 October 2018. In this case, the reporting
agent still reports the instrument for reporting reference date 31 December 2018.
The reporting agent does not report the instrument as of 31 October 2018 or 30
November 2018.
For more information regarding the reporting of written-off instruments, please refer to
Section 5.2.2.2.1.

Glossary
Revision mark: the glossary is
expanded with additional
terms/acronyms
Term/acronym Description/definition
Agent: An observed agent is an institutional unit whose activity as
observed agent creditor or servicer is reported by the reporting agent. The
observed agent is either:
a) the institutional unit resident in the same country as the
reporting agent of which it forms part; or
b) a reporting agent’s foreign branch, resident in a
reporting Member State; or
c) a reporting agent’s foreign branch, non-resident in a
reporting Member State.
[Article 1(9) of the AnaCredit Regulation]
Agent: A reporting agent is either a credit institution or a foreign branch
reporting agent of a credit institution that is resident in a reporting Member
State and that is subject to the ECBs reporting requirements
pursuant to the AnaCredit Regulation (Regulation (EU) No
2016/867).
[Article 1(8) of the AnaCredit Regulation]
Branch: A branch office is an individual place of business which forms a
branch office legally dependent part of an institution and which carries out
directly all or some of the transactions inherent in the business
of the institution.
[Article 4(1)(17) of Regulation (EU) No 575/2013]
Branch: A foreign branch is an institutional unit which is a legally
foreign branch dependent part of a legal entity resident in a different country to
that where the legal entity is incorporated in accordance with
the concept of a “single branch” referred to in Article 2(3) of
Regulation (EC) No 2533/98.
[Article 1(4) of the AnaCredit Regulation]
Branch: A resident foreign branch of a credit institution is a foreign
resident foreign branch (see foreign branch above) operating within a reporting
branch of a Member State, of either a resident credit institution or a credit
credit institution resident outside of any reporting Member States.
institution
Branch: A single branch is any number of branch offices set up in the
single branch same country. See also institutional unit below.
[Article 2(3) of Regulation (EC) No 2533/98]
Commitment The commitment amount of an instrument is the sum of the
amount data attributes “outstanding nominal amount” and “off-balance-
sheet amount” of the instrument at a given date.
[Article 1(25) of the AnaCredit Regulation]

to take deposits or other repayable funds from the public and to

Credit risk Credit risk is the risk that a counterparty will fail to make any
